Lawyer Shen Xiaoxiang has been practicing law in Fujian for eight years. On June 21, his registration with the Jiangsu High Court was approved and reported to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for record. All levels of courts in Shanghai have been notified. He has applied to join the Shanghai Bar Association and is scheduled to resume practicing law on July 21. He will establish a general legal office at No. 10 Songshan Road (formerly Glo Road).

News from Nanyang Bridge Clinic 168

Xu Xiuting, Lin Zhengtang, Ye Ruizhai, and others from the business community of Nanyang Bridge, in the French Concession, established a free clinic in the Nanyang Bridge Business Association to benefit the poor and sick in the summer when diseases are prevalent. They have two departments, Chinese and Western medicine, and have hired Chinese medicine practitioners Chen Shimei and Zhang Zhiming, throat specialist Chen Xiqing, and Western medicine doctors Ouyang Jixuan and Zhu Jusheng. They provide daily diagnosis and treatment for internal and external medicine cases free of charge. In addition to the clinic, medicine is provided for those who are extremely poor. Since the opening of the clinic, the Western medicine department has treated over 400 cases, and the Chinese medicine department has treated hundreds of cases. Xu Xiuting, the general director of the clinic, has extended the appointment of Dr. Chen Baoshu, a doctor of feeling, to the clinic every morning due to the large number of patients seeking treatment.

Assorted News 169

Smuggling Opium: Chen Guilin, an opium smuggler from Jiangbei, was found carrying 156 taels of opium on Huangpu Road at around 9:00 AM yesterday. He was stopped by Chinese officer No. 2339, who was suspicious of his movements. The opium was found during a search. He was taken to the Hongkou Police Station along with the opium. The chief detective ordered him to be detained and sent to the Special District Court for interrogation.

Gambling Den Raid: The Chinese chief detective of the Harbin Police Station raided a gambling den at No. 360 Hailer Road yesterday afternoon. Chen Zhou, a woman from Ningbo who owns a shipping company, was arrested and taken to the police station, along with gambling documents and gambling money. She was transferred to the women's prison for temporary detention, awaiting trial in court.

Opium Den Raided: Pan Gensi, a Western chief detective from the Transportation Department, raided an opium den at No. 1041 Wuzhou Road yesterday afternoon. Wang Fugen, a local opium seller, was arrested along with the opium paraphernalia and taken to the Harbin Police Station for detention awaiting trial.

Two Serial Thieves: Han Jianming and Li Liansheng, two serial thieves, were dressed in Western clothes and acted lavishly. Last month, they successively broke into the homes of Lu Xinfu at No. 13 Dafeng Lane, Julai Road, Zhang Mingxin at No. 15 Wanyi Lane, Luban Road, Xu Guoguang at No. 10 Lanwei Ai Road, and a foreigner, Eilana, and a Korean, Pike, in the French Concession, under the pretext of renting a house. They stole expensive clothes and ornaments and fled, selling the stolen goods for money to share. The French Police Detective discovered this and arrested Han and Li, recovering the stolen goods. They were taken to the police station and sent to the French Court for trial the day before yesterday. The plaintiffs complained of the theft. The two defendants confessed to the serial theft. Chinese and Western officials sentenced Han and Li to one year each in Western prison as a warning. The stolen goods were confiscated and returned to the plaintiffs for identification.

The Story of World Literature (182) American, written by Han Masi, translated by Hu Zhongchi 175

Chapter 47: The American Novel

Mark Twain is the most original and profound American writer of all America. Howells called him the Lincoln of American literature. No other writer can compare with him in the scope of his knowledge, the knowledge he has digested and pondered, and his understanding of the variety and diversity of American life. He was born in Missouri, which was central-western and half-southern. He lived in California for a short while and in New York and Connecticut for many years. He travelled the world and knew all kinds of people and their circumstances. The idea that his wings were clipped and the dignity of American life prevented his genius from fully expressing itself is meaningless, a kind of notion recently popular among young critics. No writer was more suited to introduce the country in which he lived, and no country has ever had a writer more prepared to introduce it. He said everything he should have said, and he knew the art of saying it, and the surrounding things nurtured his genius.

He began as a journalist in Nevada and California, gaining a local reputation as a humorist. His newspaper sent him as a correspondent to travel in Europe and the Holy Land. His correspondence became his first important work, "The Innocents Abroad." This is not a comic book. It has a lot of humor. Some of the humor is inevitably shallow, but most of it is honest, independent genuine observation and reports of practical experience. The genuine segments are written in excellent prose. He discovered in some segments that, as he grew older and became more enlightened and reflective, he was accompanied by a developing aesthetic awareness. There has never been a better travel correspondent than him. His sharp eyes saw through everything. He had the genius to understand any scene and to communicate it. This special talent was demonstrated in the later "A Tramp Abroad" and "Following the Equator." In fiction, his masterpiece is "Adventures of Huckleberry Finn." This stands alone in his works, because "The Adventures of Tom Sawyer" is incomparable to it, although Mark Twain, who had no critical knowledge, seemed to prefer the smaller work to the larger one. "Adventures of Huckleberry Finn" also stands alone in American literature. There is nothing similar to it in the scope of the scene and in the variety of the story's interest. If one simply thinks of vastness, then this is not isolated in world literature, because there is at least one great humorous novel of vagrancy and adventure called "Don Quixote" that can be compared. "Adventures of Huckleberry Finn" is not just a story for young people, and although young readers read it as they love reading "Gulliver's Travels," not knowing where the deep meaning lies, this is not a book for children. Through Huck's innocent eyes, we see the entirety of civilization (or what civilization lacks). We gain an almost epic perspective on the center of American history and the geographical center of that country. In Mark Twain's light-hearted works, there is much humor and sharp observation of characters, but there are also signs of imbalance, restlessness, and impatience, as if there were missteps in the production. Almost all the value of "Pudd'nhead Wilson" lies in the "Calendar" which Mark Twain continued to use as titles for chapters of other books, and in the most acute and magnificent aphorisms that have ever been uttered. In "Joan of Arc," which can be considered a novel, there is much beauty and lasting taste. However, the best above all (after Adventures of Huckleberry Finn) are two satirical novels, "The Man That Corrupted Hadleyburg" and the wonderful fable published after his death, "The Mysterious Stranger." Mark Twain had the talent for astonishing accusations, the stinging indignation, and the chilling ability to mock what he hated, like Swift's acerbity, mixed with pity, a deep Swiftian acerbity. Often, he is most cruel when he laughs the loudest. "A Connecticut Yankee in King Arthur's Court," on the surface, is a somewhat loose comedy with a humorous flavor, but at its core, it is a study of democracy and a violent attack on the folly of mankind. There, Mark Twain expressed the desire to hang all mankind.

He is a great pamphleteer with that astonishing talent for pointing out faults, intense indignation, and a chilling way of mocking what he hates. Readers who ignore his repeatedly published protest essays are missing one of his most magnificent and admirable aspects. Much of Mark Twain's humor has gradually lost its vitality. This may be true. Some, without his other works to sustain their life, are fleeting and destined to be forgotten. However, the genuine Mark Twain is a truly immortal classic, no less than any prose writer of the same century. When he speaks directly from his heart, as in "Life on the Mississippi," without the interference of any traditional literary forms, he is a master of style. He is our laurelled prose writer of democracy – he would probably say everything about democracy.

On one side, the Californian side, linked to Mark Twain is Bret Harte. He developed the life of the pioneers of the West Coast for the enjoyment of readers on the East Coast, and he did it brilliantly. His gamblers and miners are sentimentalized. He seems to have learned something from the most flawed part of Dickens's genius. However, he wrote beautiful prose. He knew the art of the short story, and he was clever in his approach to romantic emotions. He was extremely prolific. Most of his works have been forgotten. However, novels like "The Luck of Roaring Camp" are still fresh. One of his works, I believe, will not be forgotten, because it is excellent humor and first-rate indirect literary criticism. That work is the two-volume "Condensed Novels."

Page 22

Book Review

Her News, Sweet Grass 176

Written by He Yubo

Published by Modern Bookstore

In the recent literary scene, we don't see any new works that are worth noting. Yesterday, I saw this book of creations in the library, and it immediately made me feel infinitely soaring. With a light, clear, tactful and graceful pen, it depicts several poignant stories. I find this book satisfactory.

Inside are eight short stories. The author's style is very delicate and refined. The first one is "Birds of the Same Fate," which depicts a young student who falls in love with a prostitute. Later, the student becomes impoverished and desperate, and is mistreated by the madam in a foreign land. However, the prostitute genuinely loves him. Later, the prostitute argues with the madam and commits suicide. At the same time, the poor, desperate, and with no way out, the student falls ill in the hospital. He sees this news in the newspaper and also embraces death, leaving the real world.

This piece expresses deep sympathy for the modern youth's distress, sexual expression, and people groaning in the vortex of the times. When the rosy dream is shattered by poverty, the past pavilion suddenly disappears, how does the heart regret itself? The student and the prostitute argue and then go to their desolate residence, where they have self-reflection and affirmative repentance.

A brothel can no longer be considered a person, but a machine for manufacturing flesh. They have to treat guests insincerely for money. In fact, it is difficult to blame them. They are just like mules and horses pulling carts on the road, only for others to drive.

A pimp is like the cargo on a cart. The shopkeeper and head of the brothel are like merchants or capitalists. The aunts, fellows, and other people are like the servants who drive the cart. In this situation, how can the pimp get any comfort from the brothel, which is like a mule and horse? He is just sitting on the cart, unknowingly creating a lot of profit for the merchants or capitalists who use women as mules and horses. If this kind of cargo has no profit to be made, they will not transport it either.

This analogy is very apt and can make people understand the real situation in the brothel.

The second is "Leaving Beijing," which is the sorrow of parting when leaving the capital city. At the same time, it vividly reveals the modern people's hard life. The third is "Regimental Commander's Wife." The cruelty of the warlords. The warlords are bandits. It is written very painfully. Killing and looting, breaking up young unmarried couples, and forcibly occupying other people's wives. The fourth is "Bankruptcy," which describes the poor social organization and the suffering of the people caused by the warlords, making a lively young person step into society and unable to find a good job. It is like a cruel sword that turns a good family into utter ruin. At the same time, it gives deep sympathy to the vicissitudes of life and the coldness of human feelings. The fifth is "After the Divorce." This piece is about the love of a rural elementary school teacher. This piece has received such criticism from Zhao Jingshen and is indeed worthy of praise and exclamation.

Zhao Jingshen said in the third section of the first preface:

If we compare "After the Divorce" with "Regimental Commander's Wife," "Leaving Beijing," "Bankruptcy," "Her News," "Suicide," "Election" and other pieces, we will be even more surprised. A novel depicting love in a rural setting like "After the Divorce" can be compared to Wang Jingzhi's "Jesus's Instructions" and Xu Jie's "Neighbors." Whether in structure or diction, it is very pleasing. If we look at the author's date of birth, we will know that "After the Divorce" is the most recent piece, which shows that the author has made rapid progress in skills. According to such a progress ratio, I think Mr. He's future is unlimited. Even if there is only this one piece, "After the Divorce," it has already made us very satisfied.

The sixth is "Her News." Living as a guest in a foreign land, separated for seven years, revisiting the old place, thinking of the past, thinking of the love with the girl in those years. Now, after seven years, I don't know what her news is. Looking at the vast waters of Dongting Lake, it seems like the graceful figure when bidding farewell in those years, leaving behind a song of lovesickness. The rhythm of emotion and the power of skill give people a resonance.

Flow, water, flow!

Flow away my youth,

Flow away my lover,

How can it not flow away my sorrow and anger,

How can it not flow away her graceful figure?

Flow, water, flow!

May it flow me to her hometown,

May it flow me to her side,

Allow me to see her,

I would like to sleep forever in your heart.

The seventh, "Suicide," is the sadness of the prostitute herself, and the first one also expresses extremely genuine sympathy for the buying and selling of current sexual desire. The eighth, "Election," this piece put a fatal blow to the unreasonable representative politics. The local tyrants and evil gentry in the countryside are extremely skilled at playing tricks in the election.

The novel is neither a pile of facts, nor is it just a beautiful screen woven with words, it is the art of life. This cannot be denied. Now, most writers either specialize in piling up their own romances, or wholeheartedly weave brocade of words. They do not know that the author should have great sympathy for all things, and from this produce correct ideas, so that appropriate words can become beautiful works.

The author of this book has an extremely serious, earnest, and sincere attitude towards creation. If he continues to work hard like this, he can hope to achieve great success in the future.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book Reviews 177

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to recent works by new writers at home and abroad and attached pictures related to the text.

(3) Photos are limited to recent portraits of writers at home and abroad and various photographs related to the text and works.
